  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a34594ba-7ec9-4838-b6b3-111d94112067'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer2024281564122254303">Alexa Hollen is a fighter.   <span id="freeText2024281564122254303" style="display:none">Alexa Hollen is a fighter. Forced to disguise herself as a boy and serve in the king's army, Alex uses her quick wit and fierce sword-fighting skills to earn a spot on the elite prince's guard. But when a powerful sorcerer sneaks into the palace in the dead of night, even Alex, who is virtually unbeatable, can't prevent him from abducting her, her fellow guard and friend Rylan, and Prince Damian, taking them through the treacherous wilds of the jungle and deep into enemy territory.<br /><br />The longer Alex is held captive with both Rylan and the prince, the more she realizes that she is not the only one who has been keeping dangerous secrets. And suddenly, after her own secret is revealed, Alex finds herself confronted with two men vying for her heart: the safe and steady Rylan, who has always cared for her, and the dark, intriguing Damian. With hidden foes lurking around every corner, is Alex strong enough to save herself and the kingdom she's sworn to protect?</span>

<a href="/questions/676232-what-age-is-this-book-appropriate-for">What age is this book appropriate for?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_676232'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F17406847-defy">like</a></span>

<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/676232-what-age-is-this-book-appropriate-for">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/676232-what-age-is-this-book-appropriate-for">See all 5 answers</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/107710553-emerald"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/107710553-emerald">Emerald</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">In terms of appropriateness, I would say that is a personal question for everyone. I am 20 and I read this book for the first time when I was 18 and i<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">In terms of appropriateness, I would say that is a personal question for everyone. I am 20 and I read this book for the first time when I was 18 and it still bothered me in terms of the violence against women. But then again, there are many books in which that is a theme (consider the popularity of the Handmaid's Tale). If you are wondering for yourself then I would say you must make the decision of whether you can handle the references to rape as well as the arc involving drug abuse (which no one seems to mention). If you are wondering for others, consider their maturity and readiness for the same features while knowing that 'everything works out in the end'.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1706439470233906791"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388647202ra/7892463.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Mulan would fucking NEVER. Screw the love triangle. Screw the overwhelming romance. This is not a fantasy book. This is a love story.</b> Don't look for anything beyond that. <br/><br/>Hearts flutters. Desire courses. Cheeks flush. Blood flows overwhelmingly to the penis instead of the brain. WHERE IS MY PROMISED MULAN?!<br/><br/>I am just so bloody tired of so-called bad-ass heroines who do fucking nothing to prove that they're capable. I am so fucking sick of heroines who spend their supposedly ass-kicking selves sob</span>
  <span id="freeText1706439470233906791" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388647202ra/7892463.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Mulan would fucking NEVER. Screw the love triangle. Screw the overwhelming romance. This is not a fantasy book. This is a love story.</b> Don't look for anything beyond that. <br><br>Hearts flutters. Desire courses. Cheeks flush. Blood flows overwhelmingly to the penis instead of the brain. WHERE IS MY PROMISED MULAN?!<br><br>I am just so bloody tired of so-called bad-ass heroines who do fucking nothing to prove that they're capable. I am so fucking sick of heroines who spend their supposedly ass-kicking selves sobbing and crying and fucking <b>feeeeeeeeeeling</b> things and checking out her fellow half-naked soldiers wondering things like, my god, how did I not notice how fucking HOT his body looks when he's dripping with sweat! It's a fucking reverse harem!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388647202ra/7892464.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let's just overlook the fact that there are fucking rape farm/breeding houses for a moment, because there are bigger problems at play here. Yeah, you heard me. <b>Breeding houses</b>. Rest assured, there will be a rant on that, with many words starting with F and ending in UCK, but for now, let's stick to the main issue at hand, which is to say, the problem with this book is the fact that <b>it is a goddamned romance and nothing more, complete with much sighing, much longing, much "I CAN SEE HIS SOUL THOUGH HIS EYES" crap and a love triangle</b>. If you took away all the breaths that goes aflutter and the pitterpatter of fucking heartbeats, this book would be around 50 pages instead of the original 300+.<br><br>I had high hopes for this book. You know why I'm making so many random Mulan references? Because that's what this book promised me, in a goddamned nutshell. Come on, now. A girl disguised as a boy, serving as a soldier. The parallels are obvious. But no. Mulan has a good head on her shoulders. <b>Alexa's head is so high up her ass that it actually reaches her heart</b>, and that's my only explanation for the overwhelming amount of romance in this book.<br><br>I wanted this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388647202ra/7892465.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I got this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388647202ra/7892466.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>Summary</u>: Alex is actually Alexa, a 17-year old girl, disguised as a 20-year old man in the army. She and her twin brother, Marcel, has been soldiers assigned to serve as Prince Damian's guards. Years ago, a foreign army invaded their land, and the only option for Alexa was to disguise herself as a boy so she could join the king's army, otherwise, she would be forced into a breeding house.<br><br>Alexa is special. Skilled. Spectacularly skilled. Blessed with extraordinary fighting skills, as her brother would say. She can even beat her bigger brother in a fight. Hell, she can beat every fucking soldier in the squad. Because she's really, really special. And talented. And Rylan, yummy Rylan with his chocolate brown eyes, thinks so, too!<br><br>Alexa is in service to Prince Damian. He's an asshole (a gorgeous asshole, naturally). He parties all day. He has women throwing themselves at him (Well, women who <i>aren't</i> in the breeding houses, that is. Still no fucking idea how that works.) Prince Damian is a complete asshole, son of the motherfucking tyrant king, but <b>Alexa knows that under his dirtbag interior, there's more to him. She can see the gentleness in his eyes, she can see it in the way he tilts his head, she can see it in the swirling pattern of the shit he takes in the outhouse.</b> The fact that he acts like a douchebag means absolutely nothing at all.<br><br>Marcel dies right away! Well, that's so fucking convenient! Because now Alexa gets to be aaaaall alone with Prince Damian! They're so close! She gets to guard his bed! She gets to be around him all the time! She gets to see him half-naked, glistening in sweat! And man, is that fucking Damian a yummy dish! MUST. STOP. BLUSHING. BECAUSE. SOLDIERS. DON'T. BLUSH.<br><br><b>She thinks he sees interest in Damian's eyes, which, to a reasonable person would mean that Damian is gay, since Alexa is under disguise as a MAN, after all, but fuck common sense, right?</b><br><br>Alexa spends days, nights guarding Damian, thinking of him, bonding with him, getting closer to him, seeing his well-defined abdominals, dreamily interpreting and overthinking every fucking thing he says and does. She gets to go on a secret mission with Rylan, the yummy chocolate-eyed guard! She gets closer to him. She feels the camaraderie---the...love? Wait, can this be love? But what about Damian! How does Alexa get close to Damian?<br><br>But then they get kidnapped! There's danger! There's intrigue! There's more opportunities for Rylan and Damian to get closer to Alexa as they travel through the hot, humid jungle! And what does heat and humidity mean? TAKE OFF YOUR CLOTHES, RYLAN AND DAMIAN! YEAH! Clothing optional: because I swear that the guys in this book spend more time half-naked than the entire pack of Forks werewolves put together. Jacob Black would be ashamed.<br><br>Does the friendly, protective Rylan mean more to Alexa than the handsome, intriguing, mysterious Prince Damian? How will Alexa ever choose?!<br><br><b>And the fate of the nation rests upon Alexa! Wait. Where the fuck did that come from?</b><br><br><u>The EMOTIONS</u>: Mulan would never fucking pull half the shit this stupid chick does. Mulan is a fucking master of disguise compared to Alexa.<br><br>This is me (in a very unfortunate sparkly photo booth): <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388647202i/7892467.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I would actually be a more convincing man than Alexa, because half the fucking cast guesses that she's a girl. Why? SHE BLUSHES, SHE FLUSHES, HER HEART FLUTTERS, SHE GETS FLUSTERED. Soldiers would never. Mulan would never! Let's see, throughout the book. Alexa can hardly <i>"keep from blushing</i>. <i>"[Her] heartbeat was probably visible in [her neck], it was pounding so hard."</i> Her neck grows hot. Her cheeks flush. Her heartbeat flutters. Her emotions are welling underneath the surface. FUCKING ENOUGH ALREADY. Is all this shit supposed to prove to me that you are a fucking warrior? I don't bloody think so.<br><br>I understand the need to be feminine, that feminity does not disappear under the guise of a man. That clothing does not hide who you are, regardless, there is a fucking time and place for your fucking emotions and your thoughts of romantic love, so leave that shit elsewhere because I don't fucking want it. <b>I want a bad-ass heroine who knows her duty. I want a kick-ass chick who can suppress her emotions enough to get shit done.</b> Alexa proves to me nothing. Throughout her painful narrative, all I got from Alexa is a girl who wants to frolic in a field of flowers with her douchebag prince while her fellow soldier stands posing half-naked on the side. I see a girl whose emotions, whose need for romance gets the better of her, and really, fuck that shit. It has no place in a book where the plot is supposed to be important.<br><br>Her emotions. ALEXA'S FUCKING EMOTIONS FOR HER LOVER(S). They are all over the goddamned place. Is it a problem? YES, IT IS. She shouldn't be focusing on whether she's falling in love with Prince Damian or Rylan when her identity is at stake, when a war is in progress, when the fate of so many people lies in question. Alexa can't seem to think beyond her needs and her feeeeeeeeelings. Want some examples? I'll give you some examples. <br><br><b>Her heart</b> beats, <b>oh, how her fucking heart beats all the fucking time</b>, so much that I just wanted to rip it from her stupid fucking chest. Alexa's heart (all quotes from the book) "pounds" (many times), "constricts," "beats erratically," "thudded," "skipped a beat," "lurched unwittingly," "beats harder," "raced," "jumped into her throat," "skids a bit," "leaped into her throat," "beat unevenly," "raced," "constricted," "pounded," "<b>"flopped like a wounded animal,</b>" "leaped into my throat." Ok, I'll stop there. That's around half the book. HALF. THE. BOOK.<br><br><b>Her blood</b>: "pulsed hot through her veins", "pulsed hot through her body" (several times).<br><br><b>Her cheeks</b>: "felt flushed" "blushed" (so many times), "grew warm with shame," "flamed" (multiple times), "burned," "grew hot again," "grows hot."<br><br>She cries. She bawls. She runs away when her emotions for the two guys get the better of her (when they're in the motherfucking jungle). Her eyes "burned with tears," "tears ran down her cheeks," she "swallows her tears." She's a fucking Kleenex commercial. She cries so many times that I frankly got sick of it. I don't fucking care. I understand that emotions get the better of people sometimes, but seriously, choke it down. I want a warrior who can control her emotions. <b>I don't want you to cry like a motherfucking pussy when the boy you love lies to you.</b><br><br>Her priorities are just plain fucking wrong. In the middle of the fucking forest, she wonders: <blockquote>
  <i>This is a disaster.</i>
</blockquote>Oh! Yay! A disaster! Why is it a disaster? I can think of a few reasons why, because they're kind of in a precarious situation. Like they were just kidnapped, they're traveling in the jungle. They're afraid for their lives. Surely, THIS IS THE DISASTER TO WHICH ALEXA IS REFERRING.<br><br>Wrong. Why is it a disaster?<blockquote>
  <i>[Rylan] wouldn't meet my gaze, and my stomach clenched. But Damian looked straight at me, and his expression was one of confusion, even hurt.</i>
</blockquote>ARE. YOU. FUCKING. KIDDING. ME? <b>Your life is in danger, and you're concerned about two boys fighting over you like two alpha wolves fighting over which tree they get to fucking piss on first?</b><br><br>Mulan would fucking NEVER.<br><br><u>The Setting</u>: Rape houses?! Really? Fucking seriously? WHY?! I might understand it if there was a reason behind it, if there was a compelling plot issue behind it, but no. <b>The inclusion of the rape/breeding houses was absolutely pointless</b>. It is mentioned only several times throughout the book. Seriously, it is pointless. It is a tool of fear, and I hate the fact that sexual violence is used as the major threat of oppression. There are so many factors at play in a crual regime such as this, and there was absolutely no point to the rape houses.<br><br>So there actually was a point to the rape houses, according to the book. <b>They are used to breed soldiers.</b> What the actual FUCK, people? That doesn't even fucking make sense. According to the book, the king's evil war-bound regime started somewhere around the time of Alexa's birth, which wasn't even fucking 20 years ago. In all that time, the only tool in his arsenal to create more soldiers is to make breeding houses, where women are imprisoned as soon as they get their first period and are forced to spend their entire fertile lives breeding new soldiers for the king's army?! That makes no fucking sense. You could kidnap soldiers from other countries. You could train your own soldiers really well. Or you could piss off your fucking entire nation and invest 10-15 years into a war that you are losing while you're waiting for your future army to grow up? Seriously?!<br><br>Children are not sprung forth from Zeus' forehead, fully grown, fully fucking able to fight. This ain't Greek mythology, these are people, not gods. Even if you wanted fucking child soldiers, it would take 10-15 years to get them anywhere ready to fight. And to piss off your entire nation like that? Why?! You are fucking all your people (literally and figuratively) for no reason at all. You fucking expect me to believe that? That men are willing to send their wives, daughters, sisters, nieces, off into these houses to be raped their entire lives, to be killed by childbirth, be terrorized, and do absolutely jack shit about it? <b>How fucking dumb do you think I am?</b><br><br>Take a culture of extremism. Take Afghanistan. Take the Taliban. Yeah, they oppress their women. They don't educate them. But do you really fucking think that all the men would do nothing if all their women were taken away to be raped constantly? I don't fucking think so. There is always a line.<br><br>And this concept isn't even constant. The setting itself is so poorly done. You have 3 nations, one of them is a quasi-Chinese one, and all of them are so poorly described that I have no sense of nationality, no sense of what differentiates them, no sense of why they are fighting amongst each other. I don't know their society. We are mainly in the country of Antion. I know nothing of Antion culture. I know nothing of Antion history. I know nothing about the people of Antion besides the fact that they are constantly at way.<br><br>Think of it this way, I am neophyte to geography, to history. You give me 3 nations: Ireland, England, Wales. How the FUCK do I distinguish between them if I know nothing about them but the fact that they're relatively close to each other? The world building is so incredibly vague in this book. There is largely no history, there is no explanation for anything. The magical system is completely basic, BOOM! Magic! Some people haz it, some people don't! There you go! Take it, swallow it, be thankful for it because you ain't given any more than that.<br><br>I don't know how and WHY certain women are allowed to go around dancing in the court and fucking Prince Damian while the rest (god knows how many they are) are forced into these breeding houses. Screw this world. It is faker than Kim Kardashian's plastic ass, just as believable (and nowhere as inviting).<br><br><u>The Romance</u>: FUCK THAT LOVE TRIANGLE. FUCK THAT. The entire book is filled to the brim of Alexa's wavering heart between the unfortunate friend-zoned Rylan and the douchetastic Prince Damian, who has an "exquisite exterior," as well as an exquisite posterior. The entire book is filled with Rylar's pained protestations of love (love, not like) for Alexa, and Prince Damian's runs-cold-then-hot gestures of love (love, not like) for Alexa. Love! Love! LOVE! SOOOOOOOOOO much love. She admires their well-muscled body, their shirtless moments, seriously, the guys in <i>Playgirl</i> wear more clothing than Damian and Rylan. <blockquote>
  <i>"I almost cried again. I could no longer deny that I was falling for him---so fast and so hard it scared me. But I had feelings for Rylan, too---he was the closest friend I'd had at the palace."</i>
</blockquote>Priorities. Why do you not have them, Alexa? You have a motherfucking country to save.<br><br>Alexa is a psychic. Well, actually, she's not a psychic, but I'm convinced she is one. You see, she feeeeels things. She seeeeeees things. Prince Damian is a douche. He has always been a douche, but in his eyes, Alexa sees that there's something more. She sees that he's a kindly person because his eyes says so. She feels that he is a gentle soul because of the way he bends his head. She sees that he loves bunnies, puppies, and small children according to the way he hesitates before talking to her. <b>She knows that underneath his cruel front, Prince Damian is the king the country needs, because his farts smell like Calvin Klein Eternity.</b><br><br><b>STOP SEEING STUPID SHIT IN PEOPLE'S EYES</b>. Actions! Actions speak louder than words, people. I hate it when people seeeeees through others' souls in books. Eyes tell you nothing. I once dated a guy who told me that we were meant to be together. He said that he knew I felt the same way, because my eyes were looking into his soul.<br><br>I was actually thinking of what I would be doing that night when I got home and played on my priest character in World of Warcraft. That was our last date.<br><br>The end.<br><br><i>I received this book as an Advance Reader Copy. All quotes were taken from an uncorrected galley and is subject to change in the final edition</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1706439470233906791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_762826127" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/762826127" />
    <a title="Summer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14778159-summer"><img alt="Summer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574406694p2/14778159.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/762826127?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Summer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Summer" href="/user/show/14778159-summer">Summer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people I hate</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14778159-summer?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14778159-summer?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14778159-summer?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss">netgalley-edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer762826127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14117059924220667159"><b>Edit:</b> Huh. I can't believe I didn't go over this, but the issue on the rape houses? Yeah, that was another pointless addition to a pointless book.<br/><br/><i>*Thank you Scholastic for sending me this copy via Netgalley.*</i><br/><br/>Blergh. DNF at 85%.<br/><br/>More times than I care to count, YA novels usually gain a lower rating from me due to the romance. More specifically, when the romance takes over the plot. Even more specifically, when the <b>
  <i>love triangle takes over the plot.</i>
</b> <br/>Grrr.<br/><br/>This book had so much potential. <i>So much</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14117059924220667159" style="display:none"><b>Edit:</b> Huh. I can't believe I didn't go over this, but the issue on the rape houses? Yeah, that was another pointless addition to a pointless book.<br /><br /><i>*Thank you Scholastic for sending me this copy via Netgalley.*</i><br /><br />Blergh. DNF at 85%.<br /><br />More times than I care to count, YA novels usually gain a lower rating from me due to the romance. More specifically, when the romance takes over the plot. Even more specifically, when the <b>
  <i>love triangle takes over the plot.</i>
</b> <br />Grrr.<br /><br />This book had so much potential. <i>So much.</i> What drew me in was the fact that the heroine is disguised as a guy, and is right under the king’s nose as being part of his Royal Guard. Add in some magic, sorcery, and a seemingly <i>good</i> romance, you'd think I'd love this. Right? Right? <br />Nope. <br /><br />By the time everyone found out she was in fact a girl disguised as a guy, things went a bit haywire from there. I began to dread reading the novel as the story progressed.<br /><br />I don’t give a crap if the writing is flawless (which it wasn't), or if the characterization was excellent (which it wasn’t); if the plot is almost nonexistent or taken over by romance, this equation will always be applicable:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>NO PLOT= VERY ANGRY SUMMER.</b>
</blockquote><br />Before I go into my loathing of the romance, let me delve into the character development. Or lack of it, I should say. See, the heroine Alexa was a very strong-willed, loyal girl at the beginning of the novel, whom I admired greatly. As the story progressed, she became a whiny, self-pitying shell of her former self who spent most of her time trying to choose which guy she loves more. Oh, you poor little thing! You have two guys vying for your attention, life must be so hard, right? Kill me now. Besides her, no one else was developed very well. <br /><br /><i>Defy</i> is supposed to be a high fantasy novel, based on the impression I got by reading the synopsis. Would I believe this based on the actual novel? Nope. There was little world building, so little that the only thing I know about Alexa’s world is that there is a deadly jungle located somewhere in the country (was it even a country?). That, and the vague references to sorcery and magic pretty much constituted my idea of the world. <br /><br />If those were my only two issues, I would have given <i>Defy</i> two stars. Suffice to say, they weren’t my only issues. <br /><br />Alexa is trapped in a love triangle between a snotty prince and a loyal best friend. Much like her YA heroine counterparts, it’s pretty obvious who she chose.<br /><br />I mean, based on the 85% I read, she had already declared her love for the prince. To add to that stupidity, she chose the guy who <i>repeatedly</i> <b>deceived her, lied to her, and tricked her into doing what he wanted her to do.</b> Really, why should she choose the guy who was loyal to her his whole life, who stood by her when she abandoned him, and who always defended her?<br /><br />On top of this, nothing really happened until about 2/3 of the way through, and even that was boring. I’m not entirely certain where the “action” and “intrigue” hinted at in the synopsis came from. <br /><br />Alexa is a Mary Sue, and I do not use this term lightly. She is a speshul girl with magical powers, an undefeatable swordsman, and has the attention of the freaking King’s son. Can you get any more Mary Sue than that?<br /><br />I was expecting more of a Crown of Midnight-ish high-fantasy novel; instead, I was stuck with a sappy teen romance with very little attention given to much else.<br /><br />Seriously, you’re better off watching Mulan. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14117059924220667159" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_586326289" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/586326289" />
    <a title="Gillian Berry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13535966-gillian-berry"><img alt="Gillian Berry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354328337p2/13535966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/586326289?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gillian Berry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gillian Berry" href="/user/show/13535966-gillian-berry">Gillian Berry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545597586" href="/book/show/17981400-defy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=arcs-i-own">arcs-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=world-building-woes">world-building-woes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=great-shelf-of-meh">great-shelf-of-meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=love-triangles-are-pointy">love-triangles-are-pointy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=carboard-characters">carboard-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=premise-is-perfection">premise-is-perfection</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=this-is-not-how-you-book">this-is-not-how-you-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer586326289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1728214554659536707"><br/>*sad trombone*<br/><br/> <a href='http://gillianeberry.blogspot.com/2013/12/review-defy-by-sara-b-larson.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Originally posted at Writer of Wrongs</a><br/><br/>I'm having such a hard time writing this review for multiple reasons, the main one being that I wanted to love this. I wanted so BADLY to love this.<br/><br/>I make it no secret that genderbending is one of my favorite tropes on the entire planet. <a href='http://gillianeberry.blogspot.com/2013/10/gender-bending-and-why-its-awesome.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>I wrote a whole post about it</a>. The second I read about a girl disguised as a boy in a synopsis (have yet to find a good<i> boy-disguised-as-girl </i>book, but ONE DAY).<br/><br/><img alt='Just watched Mulan. and this scene came up where the 3 soldier discuised as woman... Soon after they revel there identity and take out the fruits they used as t' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387560491i/7620335.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>
  <br/><br/>I want this story. Give me this story, book go</span>
  <span id="freeText1728214554659536707" style="display:none"><br>*sad trombone*<br><br> <a href="http://gillianeberry.blogspot.com/2013/12/review-defy-by-sara-b-larson.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Originally posted at Writer of Wrongs</a><br><br>I'm having such a hard time writing this review for multiple reasons, the main one being that I wanted to love this. I wanted so BADLY to love this.<br><br>I make it no secret that genderbending is one of my favorite tropes on the entire planet. <a href="http://gillianeberry.blogspot.com/2013/10/gender-bending-and-why-its-awesome.html" rel="nofollow noopener">I wrote a whole post about it</a>. The second I read about a girl disguised as a boy in a synopsis (have yet to find a good<i> boy-disguised-as-girl </i>book, but ONE DAY).<br><br><img alt="Just watched Mulan. and this scene came up where the 3 soldier discuised as woman... Soon after they revel there identity and take out the fruits they used as t" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387560491i/7620335.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>
  <br><br>I want this story. Give me this story, book gods!<br><br>This synopsis had me drooling, despite the "thrilling love triangle" bit at the top. I kind of ignored that, hoping it would be a palatable love triangle more in the vein of Alanna-George-Jon (more on <i>them</i> in a bit). While I'm not a girl who prefers her romance on the side, I'm sorry to say this angst-fest completely dominated the plot.<br><br>Which, at first, seems to be pretty good. We're introduced to Alexa, a girl whose parents are murdered (of course, but I can roll with this) and who then disguises herself as a boy to join the army, helped along by her twin brother (*side-eyes <a href="http://gillianeberry.blogspot.com/2013/05/piercefest-alanna-first-adventure.html" rel="nofollow noopener"><i>Alanna: The First Adventure</i></a>*). She chops her hair off and assumes the name "Alex". Three years later, she's part of Prince Damian's elite guard, having successfully avoided the heinous fate that befalls most girls orphaned by the war in Antion... the breeding houses.<br><br><img height="193" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387560491ra/7620336.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh, the breeding houses. Look. I like reading fantasy that deals with misogynist societies and proves how WRONG WRONG WRONG that is. I like genderbending, because it comes with this great message that girls are just as capable as guys, and isn't it STUPID for guys to only realize that after they've been tricked into thinking girls have penises. Also, when done REALLY right, it talks about how meaningless gender roles (and even gender in general--genderally speaking) should be. But Larson has set up a world in which the boys are sent to the army, and the girls are sent to the rape barracks, where they are forcibly impregnated to breed the soldiers of the future.<br><br>First off: logic fail. The war has only been going on for like ten years. That's a lot of children this budget-stretched kingdom suddenly has to feet, because I'm pretty sure those nine-year-olds aren't exactly ready to fight wicked sorcerers.<br><br>Secondly... ARGH. Okay. So Ashleigh over at the YA Kitten<a href="http://www.theyakitten.net/2013/12/16/review-defy-by-sara-b-larson/#comments" rel="nofollow noopener"> expressed all the reasons</a> she didn't like the inclusion of this. My issue is that the inclusion of these rape houses seems almost gratuitous. The king needs to be evil, so he's started <i>this</i>. Alexa needs a reason to be frightened to be a girl, so <i>this</i> exists. Alexa needs a motivation, and the menfolk who hate the rape houses need to be shown to be heroes, so they all hate <i>this</i>. The women in this story are either victims, or they're Alexa. Rape is not a plot point or a world-building device. It is not something that happens to other people more than the victim. This book had the potential to be fantastically feminist, and it certainly tried to be, but it missed the mark.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387560491ra/7620337.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alexa begins with integrity and actually seemed like an interesting character to start. She plays it very close to the ves, and the juxtaposition of what she's feeling with how others perceive her was interesting to me. I even felt for her, particularly in a certain affecting death scene that I liked for plot reasons but that is extraordinarily poorly executed. The writing in this book is overwrought and ungainly at times. It would veer between authentically fantasy-esque and abruptly contemporary. Also, Alexa? I ever hear you use the word "harlot" again, I'm going to punch you. But then Alexa loses her awesome. Why? <i>Because boys</i>. <br><br>And now I get to talk about the love triangle. Nooooooooo. NOOOOOOO. <i>Noooooooooo</i>.<br><br>And now I am done talking about the love triangle.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387560701i/7620362.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Spoiler: this did not happen, but wouldn't THAT have been fun!<br><br>Okay, no, I'll explain. It's eye-roll inducing. I can guarantee you there will be tons of people who will love this, but I, sadly, am not one of them. I rolled my eyes so hard I sprained them.In this corner we have Rylan, who was tragically born without a personality but luckily has warm chocolate eyes to compensate. Take a shot every time the word chocolate is mentioned in reference to his eyes! In this ring, we have Damon Salvatore Prince Damian. He has dark hair, blue eyes, a tortured past, lots of secrets, and a rockin' bod. Take a shot every time Alexa gets lost in the blue of his eyes.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387560701ra/7620363.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Do you want to know one of the reasons I love girl-disguised-as-boy stories? The gender reveal. The WTF moment. The moment a character's entire perception of he MC changes. The two "SURPRISE! BOOBS!" scenes in the <i>Alanna</i> series by Tamora Pierce, a clear influence in the creation of this novel, remain two of my favorite scenes in history. We're cheated this. Why? <b>SPOILER that is not that big of a spoiler if you were paying ANY ATTENTION:</b> <i>Because both boys knew all along. How is that any fun?</i> That just means it's instalove all over the place! They've both been in love with her since day one!<b> END SPOILER</b> And now she must chooooose, between brown eyes and blue, a boy who's safe and a boy who makes her feeeeeel, the one who knows her secrets and the one WITH all the secrets, the one who zzzzzzzzzzzzz. Blah. The middle section, in which she is trudging through the jungle, dealing with her FEEEEELINGS for both of her boyfriends, is positively turgid. It's all angst and no plot. It is the Harry Potter puppet pal beating his head against the wall. It was long.<br><br>The genderbending is pointless if you don't ever actually SAY anything about gender roles. If you don't subvert them, challenge them, or force others to rethink them. And in <i>Defy</i>, the entire conceit is pointless. It mostly made me frustrated, annoyed, and... yes, eye-rolly. This book stayed both too close to <i>Alanna</i> and too far. A names, a male twin, a dark-haired blue-eyed prince in love with the secretly female best swordsman in the palace-- all elements from both books. But <i>Defy</i> lacks the message, the fun, and the SHIPS. It lacks the girl power. It lacks the <i>eff you, stereotypes, women are not weaker</i> moment. To put it simply, it lacks.<br><br>Points for the scene in which Alex is forced to sleep wedged between Damian and Rylan. I laughed heartily for the awkwardness. (Before the cheesy conquered. Oh, lordy.)<br><br>Also... why are the native people, aka ALL of the main characters in <i>Defy</i>, white? I know this is fantasy, and you can do whatever the heck you want, but Antion is a country covered in jungle. It has mangos, macaws, and acai berries. There are jaguars. This seemed like a fabulous opportunity to include some diversity in fantasy, a genre which has historically been extremely whitewashed, but alas, Alexa's "olive skin" were as POC-y as it got. The world-building was extremely thin and the same vaguely medieval European system, just in a jungle. Like so much of the rest of the book, it was a wasted opportunity. As is the plot, which is disappointingly simplistic for an epic fantasy novel. I am curious about what the plot could be in the second book, but not curious enough.<br><br>Also, Blevon is a stupid name for a country. As is Blevonese.<br><br>Siiiiiiiiigh.<br><br><img height="222" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387560491ra/7620339.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>
</span>
  <a data-text-id="1728214554659536707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer790704402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9433313852871449326"><br/><b>ROUNDING UP TO 1.5 STARS.</b><br/><br/>Why i thought this would be a really good book i have no idea. Got my hopes to high for this one, and look where it got me.<br/>Why do i do this to myself?<br/><br/><a target='_blank' href='https://imageshack.com/i/0r7ioag' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390247430ra/8175886.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>It actually started really good! At the beginning <i>'4 stars!'</i> was constantly popping up in my head. <br/><br/><a target='_blank' href='https://imageshack.com/i/nsklqvg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390247430ra/8175887.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>This is, like, a retelling of Mulan (<--- if you haven't seen that dinsey movie what are you doing with your life?), and i am shocked it wasn't mentioned at all (in the synopsis, on the book cover, ect). Did the author</span>
  <span id="freeText9433313852871449326" style="display:none"><br><b>ROUNDING UP TO 1.5 STARS.</b><br><br>Why i thought this would be a really good book i have no idea. Got my hopes to high for this one, and look where it got me.<br>Why do i do this to myself?<br><br><a target="_blank" href="https://imageshack.com/i/0r7ioag" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390247430ra/8175886.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>It actually started really good! At the beginning <i>'4 stars!'</i> was constantly popping up in my head. <br><br><a target="_blank" href="https://imageshack.com/i/nsklqvg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390247430ra/8175887.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This is, like, a retelling of Mulan (&lt;--- if you haven't seen that dinsey movie what are you doing with your life?), and i am shocked it wasn't mentioned at all (in the synopsis, on the book cover, ect). Did the author think we would not link the two together?<br><br><a target="_blank" href="https://imageshack.com/i/0b2rudj" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390247430i/8175888.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Alexa is a fighter, she has been one since she was a small child. But when war breaks over between the 2 kingdoms, Blevonese and Antion, she watches as the soldiers kill her parents. Her brother and herself are the only ones who survive out of her family. <br>The soldiers take the little girls to a Breeding house, a terrible place where the girls are raped and forced to breed children for the King's army, but before they are able to take Alexa, her twin brother (Marcel) quickly comes up with the idea of disguising her as a boy. <br>Because they are twins all Alexa has to do is cut her long her.<br><br><a target="_blank" href="https://imageshack.com/i/nadpvsj" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390247430i/8175889._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>(see the evidence and similarity so far?)<br><br>Now, some 10 years later, Alexa is known as 21 year old boy named Alex (really she is 17), and is a personal guard to the Antion Prince - Damian. She's the best. But even she cannot defeat the powerful sorcerer who sneaks into the castle and abducts the prince, herself, and her best friend Rylan into the wilds of the jungle.<br><br>The longer she is kept there the sooner she realizes she isn't the only one with secrets...and one of them is the unmistakable attraction towards Damian, the prince. <br><b>But war is getting out of control...does Alex have the courage and what it takes to end it once and for all?</b><br><br><a target="_blank" href="https://imageshack.com/i/4jvy0nj" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390247430i/8175890._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This is 'supposedly' a 'FANTASY' debut novel. I personally think even <b>mentioning</b> the word 'fantasy' in this case is a really offensive thing towards the literature. <br>Let me tell you the truth, <b>THIS.IS.A.YA.ROMANCE.</b> debut novel, a super shitty one at that (but we will get to that later).<br>Kingdoms, kings, princes and swords do not make a true fantasy novel, and they never will! In fact, if not for all of the things i just listed, i would think without a doubt that this is set in the modern times. <br><br><pre>'....or what shade of <u>chocolate</u> his skin and <br>irises resembled.'</pre> <br><br><b>CHOCOLATE DID NOT EXIST</b> in eras and worlds like that. By the way - this is the protagonist's POV, so we are inside her head and firstly, she shouldn't even know what chocolate is.<br>Can you picture a soldier just casually unwrapping and eating chocolate? It just doesn't go right, and if the author would be bothered to do some research before starting a <s>'fantasy'</s> novel she would know that too. Scratch that, listening in history lessons would do the job just as brilliantly. <br>And the author mentioned it not only once and on PAGE 9, but also twice, on page 38!!!! <br><br><a target="_blank" href="https://imageshack.com/i/mvz1dg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390248819ra/8176104.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <u>Alexa;</u>
</b> At the beginning i really liked her; i thought she was a great and strong protagonist who made it through hell and got out being even more tougher. She managed the pretence of acting like a man for most of her life, and didn't break down in front of anyone <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ even at her brother's funeral! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and she also made her voice deepen so it didn't sound too feminin. Gotta respect a girl for that!<br>That was <b>UNTIL</b>, not even a quarter through the book, she <b>COMPLETELY</b> reversed her character personality. Alexa became this silly little girl crying for no freaking reason....<br><br><pre>...but i knew it wasn't the love he wanted <br>me to feel. Tears filled my eyes, <br>blurring him.'</pre><br><br><a target="_blank" href="https://imageshack.com/i/5nvrtjg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390254268ra/8177250.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>(That was just one of many scenes when she was crying. A soldier like her should be as tough as iron. Not cry because she hurt a guy's feelings).<br><br><b>
  <u>Damian;</u>
</b> Damian is the 'spoiled, disrespectful royal brat' whom pretty much everyone hates. That includes our protagonist, Alexa. But he also is a good actor (clue: he is even better from Alexa herself!), and pretends to be someone he isn't. Since they are both kidnapped (along with Rylan), Alexa gets to spend more time with him and <i>*shocker*</i> discovers that beneath all the arrogance is a good hearted guy.<br>I personally felt nothing but suspicion and mostly dislike towards him.<br><br><b>
  <u>Rylan:</u>
</b> Rylan is the <b>broken-hearted best friend of Alexa who unfortunately got friend-zoned by her</b>. I actually loved him. I think it might be safe to say that he was my <b>'favorite' </b> character. Fun, supportive and caring. <br><br><a target="_blank" href="https://imageshack.com/i/0lyc3sg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390254268ra/8177251.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <u>THE LOVE TRIANGLE</u>
</b> (are you ready for this cause i'm fired up now?).<br>The love triangle was possibly the worst thing in <i>Defy</i>. <b>It was the thing that made it go from bad, to really bad.</b><b>IT PRETTY MUCH TOOK OVER THE WHOLE BOOK, and made it into more of a cheesy and sappy love story that sucked major ass.</b> I did NOT FEEL the chemistry between Damian and Alexa, the <b>author</b> tells us there is 'something going on between them' and that they have the 'hots' for each other. <br>When Alexa said to Damian she 'loved him' and he said he 'cared' i laughed out loud. <br>I was rooting for Rylan, but me being mad that Alexa might as well write 'Damian is the one and only' and stick it on her ass AND forehead to make it even more loud and clear, had nothing to do why this love triangle sucked. It had more to do with <b>me not caring about all the love crap and characters. </b><br><br><a target="_blank" href="https://imageshack.com/i/14xw2g" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390254268ra/8177252.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <u>The world&gt;</u>
</b> <i>Sara B.Larson</i> has created was below what i consider 'an ok world-building and era'. <b>The only originality i found was the Breeding House</b> i mentioned in the synopsis; i liked the idea of it but we did not get any information except what is was for. Like, why did the king need so many soldiers, and why couldn't the children be born/bred the natural way (through marriage, ect)? <b>There was nearly no background about neither of the kingdoms, or really anything for that matter. <br>There was absolutely NO information about what the people believed in (their religion). No cultures of any kind. </b><br><br><a target="_blank" href="https://imageshack.com/i/m9j002g" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390344292ra/8194907.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>The truly bad thing? The writing style.</b> This is said to be a YA novel, true? Well, whilst reading it i felt like i was reading a book for a 5 year old due to poor writing and all the unnecessary drama. Now when i think of it though, this would be <b>THE</b> perfect thing to read to little children, ideally girls due to romance, who want to get into 'fantasy'. But not for me, and what i was looking for.<br><br>The ending was over the top dramatic...<br><br><pre>"Alexa!" I heard Damian's shout moments before he<br> dropped to the ground in front of me, <br>his beautiful blue eyes bright <br>with unshed tears.</pre><br><br><a target="_blank" href="https://imageshack.com/i/mvqz3g" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390344292ra/8194908.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br> and i couldn't help me crack up at some scenes. It was so...ironic as well! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Alex crying at the end when she got scarred from the fire, and breaking up with Damian partly because of it and partly because he was crowned king. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>To add to the huge pile why <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17406847.Defy__Defy___1_" title="Defy (Defy, #1) by Sara B. Larson" rel="nofollow noopener">Defy</a> was so bad - it was also predictable and ridiculous; i had the 'plot' (if there was any) figured out since the beginning.</b><br> Because the author spent about 90% on the romance it was unrealistic too. - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Alexa thought she 'hid' her secret so well and nailed the job of acting like a man, when in reality half the people knew she was a girl since day 1 and kept it from her.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><b>
  <u>Overall;</u>
</b><br><br><a target="_blank" href="https://imageshack.com/i/ghm4sg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390344292ra/8194909.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>There is <b>no uniqueness in</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17406847.Defy__Defy___1_" title="Defy (Defy, #1) by Sara B. Larson" rel="nofollow noopener">Defy</a>, <b>world-building</b>, or an <b>actual deep</b>, <b>thoughtout</b> and <b>interesting plotline</b>. It makes me angry as there are so many talented people out there with lots more potential, originality and good ideas that still haven't published their book as they are less lucky or fortunate.<br><br>Would i recommend Defy? <i>No</i><br>Would i re-read it? <i>No</i><br>Do i want to write a long complain letter to the author? <i>Yes</i><br><br><i>Sincerely - The Critic. </i> <br><br><br><pre></pre><br><b></b><br><u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><i></i><br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_755967547" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/755967547" />
    <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday"><img alt="Ash Wednesday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379043440p2/10484016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/755967547?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash Wednesday" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">OMG NO.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=on-going-series">on-going-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=bermuda-triangle-of-lurrrve">bermuda-triangle-of-lurrrve</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=cliches">cliches</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer755967547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8292172046021708459"><i>
  <b>1.5 STARS</b>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389340312ra/8022853.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I really thought reading a non-romance Western before diving into a book as universally panned in my feed as <i>Defy</i>, I'd be able to offer a unique perspective. Because I've been sufficiently warned off from this book but I genuinely thought taking expectations out of the equation, bracing yourself for the worst… maybe it won't be so bad. <br/><br/>There's a war waging between Blevon and Antion and Alexa Hollen just lost her parents to a sorcerer. Together with her twin brother Marcel, she is fo</span>
  <span id="freeText8292172046021708459" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>1.5 STARS</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389340312ra/8022853.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really thought reading a non-romance Western before diving into a book as universally panned in my feed as <i>Defy</i>, I'd be able to offer a unique perspective. Because I've been sufficiently warned off from this book but I genuinely thought taking expectations out of the equation, bracing yourself for the worst… maybe it won't be so bad. <br><br>There's a war waging between Blevon and Antion and Alexa Hollen just lost her parents to a sorcerer. Together with her twin brother Marcel, she is forced to pretend that she's a boy in order to avoid getting sent to the king's "breeding houses" where orphan girls get raped to breed soldiers for the war. Alex/Alexa and Marcel are now part of the Prince's guards as they try to protect his arrogant and pompous ass from assassination and kidnapping.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I just shook my head, using the rag to wipe away the sweat dripping down my hairline. Kai and his women. I liked him well enough, but I was glad he didn't know I was a girl. He was attractive, I suppose taller, with his light brown hair pulled back in a ponytail and his green eyes always crinkled at the corners from a constant smile. <br><br>But if I had to pick the most handsome man on the guard, I definitely preferred Rylan's warm brown eyes. His more subdued, quiet humor. The surprising gentleness he had with animals.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br>Yup, she's got ALL THAT in her plate and her thoughts are oriented towards picking which among her colleagues is the most handsome.<br><br>And that was 25% in.<br><br>It's a wonder how she got to walk with all that lady boner she's been sporting all throughout the book. I kinda wish she went and dry humped every tree she came across just to keep these incessant thoughts at bay. Because something has to shut her up long enough to explain what's all that breeding house bizzness (why is it exactly part of the story?) and maybe <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a better mourning for the eventual demise of her brother. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>If I had to make a comparison <i>Defy</i> is the poorman's third cousin neighbor of the co-worker of your uncle's gardener of <i>Throne of Glass</i>. This book, I feel is a gross misinterpretation of what current YA fantasy trends is all about. Which should come across as comical in its failed attempt but has left me mildly <s>offended</s> concerned instead. Because someone out there thinks this is what I, as a YA fantasy reader, would enjoy. <br><br>It's an oversimplification of the formula: <b>Strong heroine with proto-feminist advocacies?</b> Alex/Alexa is the best fighter in the exclusively male Prince's Guards. She can kick everyone's ass but she doesn't think she's pretty. She's a tangle of hormones because, you know, seventeen. Obviously. <br><br><b>A love triangle between the heroine, authority figure and one of her peers?</b> Alex/Alexa is caught between the <s>abs</s> <s>pecs</s> abs and pecs of Prince Damian, her misunderstood boss who only acts like a brat but is actually philosophical and shiz and Rylan, the pretty guard who is the best among the guards but not as good as Alex/Alexa because again, feminism, yay!<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>"Everything is going to be okay, Alexa. I won't let anyone hurt you, I promise. Not even the king."<br>I stared up at him, my heart in my throat. What was wrong with me? A week ago, I wouldn't even let myself admit that I found any man attractive. And now my heart couldn't seem to remember how to beat normally whenever Rylan or Damian came near me - or when either of them touched me.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389340312ra/8022854.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Sexual tension and angst?</b> Put them all three in a tent/dungeon with Alex/Alexa making out with one guy, add a bit of kissing with <i>heated passion, tingling lips and molten desire flowing in x's veins...</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389314496ra/8019156.gif" height="250" width="230" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>while other guy pretends to sleep, crying silent tears of suffering. (To be honest, I'd probably cry too.)<br><br><b>An elaborate fantasy plot where the heroine plays a central role?</b> There's some off-hand pew-pew and magicalitism of wizards and sorcerers and spells and people dying shockingly so you could shelf this appropriately. This ofcourse has to lead to the uncovering of details of Alex/Alexa's past that will be pivotal to the climactic fight scene in the end. <br><br>Because that's what works now, right? Fuck character depth and development. Fuck logic. Fuck it all, there's a little boy carried by Damian on his shoulders while they travel doesn't that make you swoon? Doesn't that melt your cold cynical heart? Wait, what? What did you say? What's the breeding houses for? You misunderstand, this is the first book in the series, this is called leaving room for the rest of the books to grow into a bigger complexity. Who cares about that anyway when there's love, LOVE, <b>LOVE</b>?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389314496ra/8019157.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It was comical enough that the book spent its clunky middle with Alex/Alexa sorting out her emotions and feels for Damian and Rylan WHILE they were held as hostages by a "dangerous" sorcerer. But as if awakened from masturbatory thoughts, someone remembers "oh hey, this is fantasy, we should probably start putting that in too" right in the 70%-ish mark. Such that the clunky delivery got way even more clunkier as chunks of the plot get explained, rationalized and revealed in a lazy Q&amp;A manner between characters.<br><br>Is this book even trying?<br><br>Look I'm not in the habit of reading books that have been well-derided by others for the sheer fun of it. I'm afraid I'm all out of snark and creativity and I have enough enough wrinkles as it is. But I really thought there was some redeeming aspect, some silver lining, the smallest reason to give it a chance and not be so universally burned.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389314496ra/8019158.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah we're just going to leave this right back there.<br><br><a href="http://ashwednesday.booklikes.com/post/756184/everything-i-thought-it-would-be-unfortunately-" rel="nofollow noopener">Also on BookLikes.</a><br><br><i>ARC provided by Scholastic Press thru Netgalley in exchanger an honest review. Quotes may not appear in the final edition.</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8292172046021708459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_781079632" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/781079632" />
    <a title="Whitley Birks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5193512-whitley-birks"><img alt="Whitley Birks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328686493p2/5193512.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/781079632?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitley Birks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitley Birks" href="/user/show/5193512-whitley-birks">Whitley Birks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5193512-whitley-birks?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5193512-whitley-birks?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5193512-whitley-birks?shelf=anti-femininity">anti-femininity</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer781079632" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7788288334524447799"><a href='http://readingwithavengeance.tumblr.com/tagged/book-review' rel='nofollow noopener'>See more on my blog.</a><br/><br/>This book started out with one of the most horrific displays of misogyny possible, and then it carries on in a mediocre fashion after that. I probably would have finished reading the book if I hadn’t been so pissed off from the start, but it wasn’t good enough to carry me through my distaste, so I DNF-ed at about halfway through, when I realized that the main character wasn’t going to shut up about all the toned and muscled torsos around. (You’d think they were painted in neo</span>
  <span id="freeText7788288334524447799" style="display:none"><a href="http://readingwithavengeance.tumblr.com/tagged/book-review" rel="nofollow noopener">See more on my blog.</a><br /><br />This book started out with one of the most horrific displays of misogyny possible, and then it carries on in a mediocre fashion after that. I probably would have finished reading the book if I hadn’t been so pissed off from the start, but it wasn’t good enough to carry me through my distaste, so I DNF-ed at about halfway through, when I realized that the main character wasn’t going to shut up about all the toned and muscled torsos around. (You’d think they were painted in neon with how often she notices and/or stares at them. I love a nice pack of abs as much as the next girl, but in the middle of first aide is not the time for that.)<br /><br />The book opens up with Alexa’s brother deciding she needs to pretend to be a boy so that she can avoid the rape houses. Yes, you read that right. In this book, young orphaned girls are sent to “breeding houses” to be raped until they conceive and then the children are taken away to “be soldiers.”<br /><br />Let’s see how many things I can find wrong with this basic premise without even trying.<br /><br /> It’s impractical; girls in shitty conditions get pregnant, but not as often as they would when under less stress, so you’re basically shooting efficiency in the face.<br /> It’s impractical; if you need soldiers now, babies aren’t going to help. <br /> Girls can do stuff besides get pregnant. PREGNANT girls can do stuff besides BE pregnant; there’s point in keeping them all in a rape house and not doing anything. <br /> If you’re strapped for bodies and really that against sending girls to combat, send your male servants and replace them with girl servants because as I said girls are capable of doing things.<br /> It’s incredibly insulting to history; what, you think real palace servants weren’t raped and then their babies pressed into royal service? That wasn’t good enough for you? You had to make dedicated rape houses to up the drama?<br /> I CAN’T STRESS THIS ENOUGH, GIRLS CAN DO STUFF, IF YOU NEED BODIES TO DO STUFF, THEN USE THE GIRLS. The only way this makes sense from a worldbuilding standpoint is if you really can’t think of anything girls are good for except sex and childbearing.<br /> There was no point, and in the end, it came off as if the rape houses were just there to provide angst and excuse for Alexa to pretend to be a boy. So not only is it illogical as hell, but it’s being used as a cheap threat, to show that the main character is in danger without actually defiling her “purity.”<br /><br />And that’s just what I’ve got off the top of my head. So, from the word go, I’m pissed off at this book, anther in a long line of books that use rape as a cheap plot point without really actually saying anything about it.<br /><br />But there’s more. The worldbuilding in this book is terribly lacking. There’s a jungle, I guess, and they eat tropical fruits, but the rest of the world is so sparse that I really can’t picture it. Honestly, I thought that Alexa’s people were recent conquerors because so many little things followed standard pseudo-European fantasy tropes. The whole of it was tropes and jungle, that’s all you get. We can’t even get a good read on how sexism works in this country, because the only points of data we’ve got are “rape houses” and “everyone who finds out about Alexa’s gender is totally cool with it.” …what?<br /><br />The plot felt…skeletal. I was so excited about a girl pretending to be a boy in the army, because I love that shit, but everything was skipped over. The most Alexa ever had to do to hide her gender was bind her breasts, we didn’t get to see any training or any logistics about hiding, nothing. Just skip straight to the point of love triangle, because it’s not like the mechanics of hiding one’s gender is interesting, right? And Alexa didn’t seem to have a good grasp on being a boy, because she kept defaulting to stereotypes and assumptions about macho behavior, so she read like someone who had only just started hiding, instead of someone who had been doing it for three years. At that point, she should know how guys act and not freak out over the least sign of emotions as if such things are antithetical to manhood. She should have seen guys acting in all manners and known that she could do the same, but no, she’s stuck in a rut. She’s like that awkward phase (Disney) Mulan went through when she first arrived to sign up for the army, only instead of being awkward and everyone wondering what’s wrong with her, the book plays off like that’s really how guys are.<br /><br />Book, have you ever met a guy?<br /><br />The plot itself had promise, and I honestly did want to see where it went, but it kept being dolled out in tiny little drops, in between Alexa going on about muscled chests and then pretending she can’t cry over her dead brother because that’s too girly. I was too annoyed at everything in between plot points to keep reading, especially since the interesting bits were so far apart.<br /><br /><i>A galley copy was provided through NetGalley in exchange for an honesty review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7788288334524447799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/615134569" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413275441p2/10890208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/615134569?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer615134569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14123685367520222530">See more reviews at <a href='http://yamidnightreads.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>YA Midnight Reads</a><br/><br/>Despite my one star rating, I wasn’t at all disappointed with Defy. Simply because I <b>knew </b>it was going to be bad, and I went into this novel just to see how terrible it was. However, I had not expected it to be so bad that I nearly vomited in my mouth.<br/><br/>Defy checks all boxes for one of the worst fantasy books I’ve read this year. Sure, we’re only 7 days into 2014 but I can just feel like it’s going to be the worst I’ve encountered.<br/><br/>1. Fail, un-kick-ass protagoni</span>
  <span id="freeText14123685367520222530" style="display:none">See more reviews at <a href="http://yamidnightreads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Midnight Reads</a><br /><br />Despite my one star rating, I wasn’t at all disappointed with Defy. Simply because I <b>knew </b>it was going to be bad, and I went into this novel just to see how terrible it was. However, I had not expected it to be so bad that I nearly vomited in my mouth.<br /><br />Defy checks all boxes for one of the worst fantasy books I’ve read this year. Sure, we’re only 7 days into 2014 but I can just feel like it’s going to be the worst I’ve encountered.<br /><br />1. Fail, un-kick-ass protagonist? <b>Check. </b>We have Alexa (Alex) Hollen, disguised as a boy to be her brother’s twin in order to escape the breeding houses instead to be a member of Prince Damian’s personal guard. <i>Apparently</i>, Alex could beat the captain of the guard in a match but I felt that Alex was so weak. I wanted an as hard as nails chick who would kick ass in her sleep. I wanted a girl with a heart of steel. But instead I got a girl who dreams of her two love interests. I got a girl who couldn’t stop her goddamn emotions. There was this certain scene where the main characters are being attacked and Alex quickly jumps into the action, I was rather confused. Because her personality was whiny and <i>girly, </i>I totally forgot that Alex was supposed to be some heroic and kick-ass boy.<br /><br />2. Non-existent world building? <b>Check. </b>For majority of the time, I couldn’t imagine anything that the author was taking about. Just insert some castle here and jungle there, viola! I need more details, more substance. And not breeding houses.<br /><br />3. Illogical plotting? <b>Check. </b>So there’s a war that’s been going on for some 10-20 years and the evil, evil king decides to get all females who have reached the age where they can reproduce to go to these breeding (rape) houses so they can make soldiers. So basically, these lil’ infants are going to go to war. WUT? You at least have to have them grow up as well as train them which is also gonna take another 10-20 years. How the flip does that work when your nation is already losing the war? How long is this war gonna go on for? NOTHING MAKES SENSE.<br /><br />4. No history on the world the author as created? <b>Check. </b>Apart from the horrendous and irrelevant breeding houses, we don’t have much else. There’s no history of what happened to make this war begin and stuff like that. I don’t want to be thrown in the middle of a book and just left there staring into the distance. I need background information. I need to know why some people have special powers and why some don’t.<br /><br />5. Love triangle? <b>Check. </b>We have a snotty and lazy and ungrateful Prince Damian and a sweet but annoying best friend Rylan. Who does she choose? Why of course, the impossible to have, Prince Damian! *rolls eyes*<br /><br />*SPOILER*<br /><br />What makes me want to gag more is that it just happens that both love interests knew that she was a girl ever since and loved her ever since. O___O<br /><br />*END SPOILER*<br /><br />If you want a girl disguised as a guy, go for Eon or watch Mulan. Honestly. Don’t waste your time on this.<br /><p>
  <em>~Thank you Scholastic for sending me this copy!~</em>
</p></span>
