<div id="review_1795737030" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1795737030" />
    <a title="Shahad takleef" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35406752-shahad-takleef"><img alt="Shahad takleef" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513107527p2/35406752.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1795737030?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shahad takleef" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shahad takleef" href="/user/show/35406752-shahad-takleef">Shahad takleef</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1795737030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11636324131762493784"><blockquote>
  <b>“True beauty is what lies inside of us, not what the world sees. A beautiful shell that houses a vile soul becomes sullied over time. But an outer shell, imperfect as it may be, that houses a beautiful, shines with that beauty, radiating it for all who have eyes to see.” </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/>This is a Dystopian novel about Alexa , a girl who had joined the military with her twin brother disguised as a boy when she was thirteen to avoid some other horrific destiny , Its been ten years since their country had star</span>
  <span id="freeText11636324131762493784" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>“True beauty is what lies inside of us, not what the world sees. A beautiful shell that houses a vile soul becomes sullied over time. But an outer shell, imperfect as it may be, that houses a beautiful, shines with that beauty, radiating it for all who have eyes to see.” </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br />This is a Dystopian novel about Alexa , a girl who had joined the military with her twin brother disguised as a boy when she was thirteen to avoid some other horrific destiny , Its been ten years since their country had started a war against some other nation and eventually magical elements would be added to the story . <br /><br />I'm having such a hard time writing this review for multiple reasons, first of all is that I've read it a while ago i can't accurately remember what i felt about it , the second though is that I was a bit disappointed to begin with . i read this according to a rec video of underrated books by Naya Perkins , I love this girl , i usually trust her opinions and she really did love it , I thought I will do as much as she did , i didn't though . <br />when I paused Naya's video and went to read the synopsis at Goodreads , I added it to my TBR instantly , even read it only a few days after , the synopsis felt quite promising , who would fail to be reminded of <b>Mulan</b> ? , it was really good except for this <i>"thrilling love triangle"</i> bit at the top of it which made me suspicious but I kind of ignored it .<br />however , it was predictable , the type of dystopian you feel like you've already read before , its familiar because this is the way most dystopian books go , If you've read <b>Throne of Glass </b>or <b>The Study series</b> for example you'd know what to expect here , there wasn't much added. So it didn't stand out and most important of all , <b> It started with a promise and ended with boredom .</b>, though i really appreciate the end because if Alexa ended up a queen with a lame <i>married happily ever after</i> end the rating would have been much lower .<br />The world building is not that unique , The war between two nations , The evil emperor , The magic and oh yes , The jungle , there's always a jungle for some reason . <br />The characters and relationships did not strike me as something so well developed , The characters were interesting, but I didn't feel invested in them . Alexa for example was admirable , she disguises her self as a boy , manages to be a royal guards , its claimed that she's the best fighter or so , this Gender bending thing would have been totally interesting if she could pull it off , she was awesome until she started admiring everybody's eyes . How she got away with pretending to be a guy for years is beyond me. Although almost everyone knew she was a girl so obviously she was terrible at it .<br />I really did like her at the beginning but it just broke off , the character started flattening .<br />It seems that she doesn't do much mourning in case she has someone's eyes to admire , and I think for <i>" The best fighter"</i> she did much blushing and heart flattering than actually Fighting . I really think the romance took much more space than it should have had , I was totally right to get suspicious at this " thrilling love triangle " in the synopsis , i thought its a high fantasy it wont bother me much , but Oh it did . It turned out there was a whole jungle journey about choosing between brown and blue eyes . I ended up with much eye rolling than I've expected .<br />Then we would be <b>"So very much shocked"</b> to discover that she has magical powers and and she's the last hope the country has to stop the war , she is the only one who can defeat a big evil sorcerer who is apparently capable of burning an entire army of sorcerers into ashes . But not Alexa. Alexa can stop him Because …. well, because she can .<br /><br />another thing that bothered me was " the breeding houses" , I read dark books , I don't feel bad because of its mere idea as long as it serves its purpose . I get what the writer wants to tell , its the fantasy that deals with misogynist societies to proves how wrong it is , but instead it felt much unnecessary , the whole thing lacks the factor of being convincing , and if you're not much convinced it hardly means anything . the whole thing was gratuitous. <br /><br />Lets not harshly judge the book , I mean I've rated Throne of Glass three stars too , but I wasn't acrid on it , It has the very same quality as this book , the writing , the story , the world building and even the annoying love triangle , all the same , if you didn't mind any thing there and you loved it , you'd do love this one , too . Its just that I expected more of this book and anyway expectation Vs reality doesn't always have a pleasing outcome . <br /><br /><br /><a href="http://idobookish.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">READ IT HERE .</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11636324131762493784" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1901342748" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1901342748" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30472130-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572577093p2/30472130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1901342748?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/30472130-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545597586" href="/book/show/17981400-defy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30472130-julie?shelf=hate-reads">hate-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30472130-julie?shelf=owned-novels">owned-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30472130-julie?shelf=age-ya">age-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30472130-julie?shelf=gender-benders">gender-benders</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1901342748" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16631751377553290805">Book Rant on my channel: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0rf9liIgBmc'>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0rf9l...</a><br/><br/>The audiobook narrator isn't actually british?? I'm shook. Also I'm so conflicted cause I don't want to continue on with the series, but I own all the books and the covers are so freaking gorgeous. So I might continue on with the series cause I love torturing myself. I will say that I did like listening to it. I feel like if I had physically read this I probably would've ended up dnfing it. I also did like the writing and the descr</span>
  <span id="freeText16631751377553290805" style="display:none">Book Rant on my channel: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0rf9liIgBmc">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0rf9l...</a><br /><br />The audiobook narrator isn't actually british?? I'm shook. Also I'm so conflicted cause I don't want to continue on with the series, but I own all the books and the covers are so freaking gorgeous. So I might continue on with the series cause I love torturing myself. I will say that I did like listening to it. I feel like if I had physically read this I probably would've ended up dnfing it. I also did like the writing and the descriptions. I felt like I could really visualize the settings and I was sucked into the story. <br /><br />Alright so I'm going to try to be as nonspoilery as possible, but I feel like I just need to vent about everything I didn't like about this book. Okay, here we go. <br /><br />I went in really hoping to love this book. It's fantasy, it's (supposedly) got a strong female mc, and it's a gender bender which is my shit. Like the whole Mulan/She's the Man dressing up as a boy and infiltrating boy territory is something that I freaking love. I can't explain why, but I do. This book however made me fucking hate it. I think I just hated the MC so much. She was annoying and whiny. She kept repeating the same things over and over again. Exampled: "piercing blue eyes" "brown chocolate eyes" "his well muscled chest" "because I'm a girl" and so on. Like OKAY I HEARD YOU THE FIRST COUPLE TIMES I GET IT. I started out really liking this book, but then it got to the romance and.... ugh. I'll get to that later. <br /><br />First off, the world building was trash. I wanted sooo much more from it. Nothing was developed enough to make sense. Everything that happened just seemed so convenient and thrown in randomly without any thought at all. The magic was just kind of there. The ending was so rushed and I zoned out a ton of the fighting scenes while I was listening to it. Maybe everything will get explained better in the next books? I don't know. I just have a lot of questions about things. A lot of the world building and magic system was just lacking in my opinion. <br /><br />The main reason the world building was probably lacking so much is because the author spent so much time building this god awful love triangle. It didn't need to happen. I knew from the beginning who she was going to pick and I'm sure it'll stay that way for the rest of the series. She'll just continue to pull the second boy along and he of course will let himself be pulled along. It's just so fucking unnecessary. Unlike most people I don't mind love triangles AS LONG AS THEY'RE DONE WELL. This wasn't one of them. For one thing the love interests are so fucking bland. They didn't seem much different to me besides the fact that one is a prince and the other is a guard. She just kept longing after them (one more than the other <i>obviously</i>). The ENTIRE time they were traveling it was just her thinking about how much she wants the boys and her being mad about the fact that the prince kept secrets from her. Get over yourself, Alexa!!! There are bigger things happening!!! The love triangle and romance in general ruined this book for me. I groaned aloud and rolled my eyes so many times while listening to this. I could not. <br /><br />Lastly the gender norms in this was exhausting. I understand that this is a sexist society. There are literally breeding houses for all the orphaned girls. They get raped repeatedly until they become pregnant and, when they give birth, their children are taken away from them. Boys get sent away to become soldiers and girls remain at the breeding house where they wait to get their period so they can get raped and bred too. This is why our MC disguises herself as a boy. She doesn't want to be separated from her twin brother or be sent to a breeding house so she cuts of her hair. As a boy, however, she basically thinks anything she does is girly. She's all "boys don't blush," "boys can't grieve," "boys stay strong and don't show emotion" and blah blah blah. Somebody finding out her secret could mean death for her so I get why she was being so cautious, but it became so overkill after a while. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The main thing that irked me was the fact that everyone (relevant) knew she was a boy??? Obviously she's not very good at disguising herself because EVERYONE knew. It's not even explained well why. There's just throw away answers as to how they know and that's not enough for me. Also the love interests were both like "As soon as I knew you were a girl I fell in love with you" and I'm just like hmmmm.... ok. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I could probably go on, but I'll stop myself here. I think I got my main points across. I don't know if they're coherent, but the words are there. So yeah I'm continuing on with the series because I want to keep the books on my shelf. I know I'm the worst. I just really love the aesthetic. I'll hate read them cause I love to hate things. Thanks for sticking around for this whole review it was probably a big old mess.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16631751377553290805" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1191311142" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1191311142" />
    <a title="Kara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3655826-kara"><img alt="Kara" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1191311142?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kara" href="/user/show/3655826-kara">Kara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545597586" href="/book/show/17981400-defy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3655826-kara?shelf=dislikeable-characters">dislikeable-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3655826-kara?shelf=really-really-want">really-really-want</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3655826-kara?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3655826-kara?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3655826-kara?shelf=mediocre">mediocre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3655826-kara?shelf=paranormal-supernatural">paranormal-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3655826-kara?shelf=amazing-covers">amazing-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3655826-kara?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3655826-kara?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3655826-kara?shelf=magic-or-powers">magic-or-powers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1191311142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11322633884767221232">Defy, defy, defy. Even after I’ve finished it I’m still uncertain about how I feel about it. Did I like it? Yes. Did I think it was the amazing, beautiful and incredible read I thought it was going to be? Unfortunately, no. I know I will read the sequel, Ignite — and maybe I’ll enjoy it more now as I will know what to expect from it.<br/><br/>Defy was described as a lush read with a tough, kickass heroine.<br/><br/>But was it, really?<br/><br/>No . . . I didn’t think so; and actually, the worldbuilding and characters was whe</span>
  <span id="freeText11322633884767221232" style="display:none">Defy, defy, defy. Even after I’ve finished it I’m still uncertain about how I feel about it. Did I like it? Yes. Did I think it was the amazing, beautiful and incredible read I thought it was going to be? Unfortunately, no. I know I will read the sequel, Ignite — and maybe I’ll enjoy it more now as I will know what to expect from it.<br /><br />Defy was described as a lush read with a tough, kickass heroine.<br /><br />But was it, really?<br /><br />No . . . I didn’t think so; and actually, the worldbuilding and characters was where this novel fell flat, as well as the romance. Well, romances.<br /><br />Here, though, was the best thing about the novel: it was so quick and easy to read. I’ve been in a bit of a reading slump — but once I got into the story it literally took me only a few hours to devour the novel. The writing style is simple, yes, but so, so easy to read. That, I thought, was where the novel excelled in creating a page-turner, because it is so easily written.<br /><br />I truly understand where the author was trying to go with the novel, and as a fellow fantasy-writer I can appreciate it, but I felt like she missed the mark in many areas of the novel that could’ve been fantastic. Take, for example, our main character — Alexa. Or, Alex, as she’s known from the rest of her guard. In the typical sense of the word, she was “badass” and “tough” but I don’t believe that was enough to sell her character to me as a reader. She was a little . . . and I hate to say this . . . but boring. The only thing I really knew about her was that she was a good fighter. That was it. When you create a badass character, I feel as though the author needs to make her flawed in a way that makes her loveable and realistic at the same time.<br /><br />Speaking of characters, a lot of them die. Which is a common thread when it come to fantasy, right? And that’s fine; it highlights a brutal world. But when it comes to death in fantasy, you want the reader to feel it, not just witness it. And I felt for a novel that was written in first person — which is usually much more emotive than third — I didn’t feel much. Even characters that were close to our protagonist, I felt oddly disconnected to the whole thing.<br /><br />Love triangles. They can either be good — or bad. I wish, I truly wish from the bottom of my heart, wish that I could say I loved it. So in Defy our two main love interests are Rylan — one of the boys in Alexa’s guard — and Prince Damian. Not sure I really cared for either one of them. The thing that bothers me so much about love triangles is always the main character’s attitude toward them — she’s always bouncing between the two, with conflicting monologue that is tiresome to read. And, I thought that the story was too focused on the romance. If the author had pulled back on it a little I think she would have had more of a chance to expand on the world she had created — which I speak about in the next paragraph.<br /><br />Next issue I had with Defy was the worldbuilding. Or — more like it — the lack of worldbuilding. Here’s the total of what I knew of Defy’s worldbuilding: there were jungles. And a monarchy system. Jungles are cool, don’t get me wrong . . . but what else? A vague mention of “God”. WHAT GOD? This is high-fantasy, a whole new world, and I can’t just assume things about a religion that’s not even there. There was also a distinct lack of history in the world; bits and pieces of it scattered here and there, most of which was cobbled together in a confusing manner, and I didn’t really get it. Something about sorcerers? And evil people? When the worldbuilding is stretched as thin as it was in Defy it’s hard for me to look past it in a positive way. You can’t be fully involved in a world you don’t even understand. Yes, I realize this is a series, but even so, this story almost lost me at its poorly developed world.<br /><br />So, all in all, not a great high-fantasy.<br /><br />Enjoyable in some regards, but also underdeveloped.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11322633884767221232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/hGeicMZLY+SvVn3flYQoKggPz+2/JsHbwItaYCaXDLKPWhaeW83+bsivPur9cEGYsIVTLxVsFMcFVVuybwyNA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jXyNF+3iy09ikhLA9pGlGdv4KP3JItBhAIaSHaJDIZW5UHvEV5TROUsN98wjMnS/ERoCjsOL+zVzkeoa62VPkw==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText4089493841330282742" style="display:none">Sara B. Larson is the best-selling and critically acclaimed author of the YA fantasy DEFY trilogy (DEFY, IGNITE, and ENDURE) and the DARK BREAKS THE DAWN duology. Her next YA fantasy, SISTERS OF SHADOW AND LIGHT, comes out November 5th from Tor Teen. She can’t remember a time when she didn’t write books—although she now uses a computer instead of a Little Mermaid notebook. Sara lives in Utah with her husband, their four children, and their Maltese, Loki. She writes in brief snippets throughout the day and the quiet hours when most people are sleeping. Her husband claims she should have a degree in “the art of multitasking.” When she’s not mothering or writing, you can often find her at the gym repenting for her sugar addiction.<br /> <br />She’s online at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.SaraBLarson.com">www.SaraBLarson.com</a>. <br /><br /></span>
